  '.__/=================================================================\__.'

The catalog is where I'll, well... catalog all of the items, weapons, enemies,
bosses, etc. from the game. You'll get a detailed listing for each individual
entry saying what it is, how to get it (or how to kill it), and a nice little
description. So if you're playing this game and you don't really want a full
walkthrough, you just want to know "what the heck is a Recorder and how do I
get it?", well this section should help you with that. Or if you just want to
know what things are actually called so you can stop calling Like Likes "tubey
guys", this section can help you with that, too.

   /\=====================================================================/\
  /__\---------------={  W E A P O N S   &   I T E M S  }=---------------/__\
 /\  /\                             [WEPNS]                             /\  /\
/__\/__\===============================================================/__\/__\

Below I will catalog ALL of the weapons and items that you will get and use in
this game, their various uses, how to use them, and how to get them. As a quick
note: the difference between Items and Equipment is that Items are something
you equip and use, Equipment is something that you just have on that provides
some sort of status or effect.

+---------------+
|--= WEAPONS =--|
+---------------+

NAME: WOODEN SWORD
USE: Slash enemies to bits.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Obtained from the Old Man in the cave on the starting screen at
the very beginning of the game.
DESCRIPTION: The Wooden Sword is the very first weapon you receive in the game,
and it's pretty dang crappy (just try to kill a Like Like with it). So,
ideally, you won't be using it for very long.

---------------

NAME: WHITE SWORD
USE: A sword that is twice as powerful as the Wooden Sword.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Once you have six or more hearts, you can talk to the Old Man
in a cave in Grid A11 and he will give you the White Sword.
DESCRIPTION: The White Sword is the sword that will get you through just about
the entire game. Considering that, it's quite effective for what you need
until you can get the Magical Sword.

---------------

NAME: MAGICAL SWORD
USE: A sword that is twice as powerful as the White Sword.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In First Quest, it is found at Grid C2 underneath a
tombstone. In Second Quest, it is found at Grid A1--0 by pushing the rock at the
tip of the arrow made of rocks.
DESCRIPTION: The most powerful sword in the game. A whopping four times more
powerful than the starting Wooden Sword, it absolutely decimates pretty much
anything that could get in your way about Hyrule. You can only obtain it after
you've obtained 12 hears on your life meter, but once you do: your life will be
a lot easier.

+-------------+
|--= ITEMS =--|
+-------------+

NAME: BLUE CANDLE
USE: Burn secret bushes to reveal passageways and the like.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Purchased for 60 Rupees from Shop One.
DESCRIPTION: The Blue Candle adds to the exploration playstyle if you want to
explore everything this game has to offer but is not necessary to just beat the
game. Still, it's pretty useful to burn down things that are blocking your
path. You can only use it once per screen though, so if you need to use it
again, you must exit and reenter.

---------------

NAME: BOMB
USE: Blow up walls, rocks, or enemies.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Dropped from defeated enemies or purchased from Shop Two or
Four.
DESCRIPTION: Bombs are perhaps THE Zelda item. They're perhaps more used as
exploration tools than weapons despite their damaging payload. They can be used
to bomb rocks and walls to reveal secret areas. You can carry 8 at a time. Bomb
Upgrades will allow you to carry 12 and then 16 later in the game.

---------------

NAME: BOOMERANG
USE: Stun enemies/Kill weaker enemies
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Eagle/E Labyrinth.
DESCRIPTION: The Boomerang is a nice weapon to have, especially for dispatching
Keese and other pesky enemies that move continuously. It can also stun larger
enemies to keep them in place while you inflict more damage with your sword.

---------------

NAME: BOW AND ARROW
USE: Shot enemies with arrows while remaining at a relatively safe distance.
HOW TO OBTAIN: From Eagle Labyrinth on the First Quest and Z Labyrinth on the
Second Quest. Arrows can be purchased from Shop Two and Four. Silver
Arrows are found in the Boss Level.
DESCRIPTION: The ultimate projectile weapon, as useful to Link as even his
sword perhaps. Once acquired, it'll be a B Box mainstay and you'll rarely have
reason to use much else. Once you get arrows, you have as much ammo as you have
rupees (firing one arrow costs one rupee). The Silver Arrow is pretty much just
a glorified regular arrow and is only used to kill Ganon.

---------------

NAME: LETTER
USE: Unlocks the ability to buy Potions from Potion Shops.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Found at Grid A15 in First quest and Grid B2 in Second Quest.
DESCRIPTION: The Letter literally has a single use: give it to an Old Lady in a
Potion Shop and they will all start selling Potion to you, enabling you to
essentially carry extra health with you from that point on.

---------------

NAME: MAGIC BOOMERANG
USE: A stronger version of the regular boomerang that flies farther.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Moon Labyrinth on First Quest and L Labyrinth on Second Quest
by defeating a specific set of Blue Goriyas.
DESCRIPTION: It's pretty much identical to the regular Boomerang other than
being able to fly farther and doing a bit more damage. That's it.

---------------

NAME: MAGICAL WAND
USE: Shoot magical energy across any room to inflict serious damage to
everything except Wizzrobes.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Dragon Labyrinth in First Quest and Morning Star Labyrinth in
Second Quest.
DESCRIPTION: The Magical Wand is the most powerful weapon in the game (that's
not a sword). Its bolts do more damage and travel faster than the Bow and
Arrow and you don't need to refill your ammo constantly. Unfortunately,
Wizzrobes are immune to it since they use the same weapon.

---------------

NAME: POTION
USE: Replenish health.
HOW TO OBTAIN: From Potion Shops after the Old Man Letter has been delivered
to one.
DESCRIPTION: Potions are absolutely must-have items once you've unlocked the
ability to buy them. Both Red and Blue Potions heal you the same amount, but
Red Potions can be consumed twice and a Blue Potion can only be consumed once.

---------------

NAME: MONSTER BAIT
USE: Used to bait Goriyas.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Purchased from Shop Three or Shop Four.
DESCRIPTION: Monster bait really servers one purpose and one purpose only: bait
Goriyas away from their path-blocking resting spots so that you can progress.
That's pretty much it, but it works for what it does.

---------------

NAME: RECORDER
USE: Shrink Digdogger and warp to various locations.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Lizard Labyrinth in First Quest and A Labyrinth in Second
Quest.
DESCRIPTION: In First Quest, the Recorder is only used to kill Digdoggers,
uncover a Labyrinth, and warp to entrances of various Labyrinths where you
have defeated the boss already. But once you start the Second Quest, it gains
the ability to uncover secret staircases through Hyrule (hint: these secret
staircases are where many of the new locations for various helpful things have
been moved to for Second Quest).

---------------

NAME: RED CANDLE
USE: A supped up version of the Blue Candle.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Demon/Spiral Labyrinth.
DESCRIPTION: The Red Candle removes the once per screen limitation of the Blue
Candle so that you can use it as much as you like/need to without needing to
exit and reenter. That being said, you'll never convince me that the only
reason that was a limitation of the Blue Candle in the first place was so they
could put the Red Candle in the game for a low-effort Labyrinth reward.

+-----------------+
|--= EQUIPMENT =--|
+-----------------+

NAME: BLUE RING
USE: Reduces incoming damage to Link by half.
HOW TO OBTAIN: At Grid D5 in the First Quest and at Grid A16 in the Second
Quest for 250 Rupees.
DESCRIPTION: The Blue Ring is absolutely NECESSARY. Pinch those rupees and make
sure you get it. You can pretty easily acquire it before going to even the
first Labyrinth. With the Blue Ring equipped, enemies will inflict half the
amount of damage they inflicted before having the ring. Once the ring is
equipped, it will turn Link's tunic blue, so you'll know it's working.

---------------

NAME: MAGIC BOOK
USE: Makes the Magical Wand shoot a more powerful blast: a FIRE blast.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Lion Labyrinth in First Quest and D Labyrinth in Second
Quest.
DESCRIPTION: NOW THAT'S A LOT OF DAMAGE! Gives the Magical Wand a huge power
up, making it do even more damage. The Magical Wand + Magic Book is definitely
not necessary for your playthrough but it's a very powerful and convenient
weapon, so I suggest going through the effort to get it.

---------------

NAME: MAGIC KEY
USE: A regular key that can be used repeatedly, removing the need to find keys
entirely.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Lion/Morning Star Labyrinth.
DESCRIPTION: The Magic Key is nice. Once you get it, you don't have to find
keys anymore, since the Magic Key works on every door. Too bad you find it in
the last Labyrinth and basically have no more locked doors to deal with anyway.

---------------

NAME: MAGICAL SHIELD
USE: Bother larger and more reinforced than the Wooden Shield.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Can be purchased from Shops One, Two, Three, or Four.

DESCRIPTION: The Magical Shield gives you the ability to block fireballs that
are thrown at you by enemies. However, be forewarned: this does not seem to
apply to Bosses. Also, Like Likes will eat your Magical Shield if they get
ahold of you.

---------------

NAME: POWER BRACELET
USE: Gives Link the ability to push, lift, and move large rocks and boulders
around Hyrule.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Found at Grid C5.
DESCRIPTION: Another must-have (boy, sure seems like just about every item is a
must-have *cough cough*) for your travels. Once you get it, you'll be able to
move large rocks and boulders which will make exploration and secret-finding
easier. You'll need it eventually so might as well get it as soon as possible,
right?

---------------

NAME: RAFT
USE: Allows you to cross bodies of water without a bridge.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Manji Labyrinth in First Quest and D Labyrinth in Second
Quest.
DESCRIPTION: The raft simply makes traversal and exploration easier by giving
you the ability to cross bodies of water from whatever point you need to. It's
also necessary since it's the only way to get to the Snake Labyrinth.

---------------

NAME: RED RING
USE: Reduces incoming damage for Link by 75%.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Final Boss Labyrinth.
DESCRIPTION: It's found in Death Mountain before your final fight with Ganon.
Absolutely get it, it makes the fight just that much easier. It also turns
Link's tunic red, which is a nice look if you like the color red.

---------------

NAME: STEPLADDER
USE: Allows you to cross bodies of water one square long.
HOW TO OBTAIN: In Snake Labyrinth in First Quest and Wizard's Hat Labyrinth in
Second Quest.
DESCRIPTION: The Stepladder is a step down from the Raft (so then it's rather
odd that you get it after the raft, but whatever I guess). It allows you to
cross the rivers in the game without needing to break out the Raft, but can't
be used for bodies of water larger than a single square. It's also a necessary
item in order to complete the Snake Labyrinth so it must be acquired!

---------------

NAME: WOODEN SHIELD
USE: Deflect projectiles and incoming attacks.
HOW TO OBTAIN: You start the game with it.
DESCRIPTION: The starter shield and not a very good one at that. It'll block
most solid incoming projectiles and that's about it. It won't block fire/energy
blasts and most boss attacks. Best to upgrade to a Magical Shield sooner rather
than later.

+--------------------+
|--= COMMON ITEMS =--|
+--------------------+

NAME: RUPEES
USE: Rupees are the in-game currency used to buy items from shops.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Rupees are dropped by enemies. Large sums of rupees can be found
in hidden areas.
DESCRIPTION: There are two types of rupees: Gold and Blue. Gold Rupees are
worth one unit and Blue Rupees are worth five. Blue Rupees are much rarer to
have drop from an enemy, but it does happen.

---------------

NAME: HEART
USE: Refills a single heart container.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Defeated enemies will drop them.
DESCRIPTION: A single, flashing heart icon that is drop by enemies when you
defeat them. They replenish one heart container, which can be useful in a
pinch. They drop about as frequently as gold rupees.

---------------

NAME: FAIRY
USE: Refills multiple heart containers at once.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Very rare drop from defeated enemies.
DESCRIPTION: Fairies are living sprites whose sole purpose is to refill your
health so that you can keep fighting the good fight. When they are dropped by
an enemy, they will fly around the screen and you have to catch them.

---------------

NAME: STOPWATCH
USE: The Stopwatch freezes all of the enemies on screen.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Stopwatches are a rare drop from defeated enemies.
DESCRIPTION: The Stopwatch can be very useful if it is dropped for you. Once
picked up, it will freeze all of the enemies around you so that you can easily
defeat them without having to worry about a counter. Link will flash when time
is frozen. Time will remain frozen until you leave the screen.

+-----------------------+
|--= LABYRINTH ITEMS =--|
+-----------------------+

NAME: MAP
USE: See the full layout of the Labyrinth.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Each Labyrinth has a map. They are hidden in various places in
their respective Labyrinths.
DESCRIPTION: The map is probably the most important item that you can find
in the Labyrinth. It's essential to know the layout of the Labyrinth and where
you are in it. Finding the map should be your first objective if you're
attempting to conquer the Labyrinth on your own.

---------------

NAME: COMPASS
USE: Shows the location of the boss on the map.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Each Labyrinth has a compass. They are hidden in various places
in their respective Labyrinths.
DESCRIPTION: The compass may not be as essential as the map, but it's always
useful to know where the boss is. You should search for the compass after
finding the map.

---------------

NAME: KEY
USE: Opens regular locked doors.
HOW TO OBTAIN: Found in various places in Labyrinths. They can also be bought
from Shop One or Five.
DESCRIPTION: The Key is necessary to progress completely through every
Labyrinth. If you are having trouble finding a key in a Labyrinth, you can
always go buy one, but make sure you look for it. Every Labyrinth has enough
hidden keys to open all of its locked doors.

   /\=====================================================================/\
  /__\-----------------------={  E N E M I E S  }=-----------------------/__\
 /\  /\                             [ENEMY]                             /\  /\
/__\/__\===============================================================/__\/__\

There are many enemies that you will come up against as you fight your way
through the land of Hyrule to face down Ganon once and for all. I've listed all
of them below along with their description, where you'll find them, and the
best strategy for dispatching them.

[enemies are in alphabetical order for the preservation of my own sanity]

+-------------+
|--= Armos =--|
+-------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A solider who has been turned into a stone statue. He moves and
attacks if touched by Link. He has a fair amount of attack power."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Really, you don't even have to fight them. They only wake up
if you attack them so they can be skipped entirely. They usually are in large
packs and you'll have to be careful to not touch any of them. If you do wake
one up, the best strategy is the slash/run/slash strategy. Hit him, run away,
hit him again.

+--------------+
|--= Bubble =--|
+--------------+

DESCRIPTION: "The spirit of the dead. When it clings onto Link, he won't be
able to unsheathe his sword for a while."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Another enemy that's better left alone. You can't damage it
with your sword, since touching it renders you incapable of using your sword at
all. There is no way to kill them.
In Second Quest, there are two new types of Bubbles: Red and Blue. Red Bubbles
will take away your sword PERMANENTLY. Blue Bubbles will give your sword back.
So, if you get hit by a Red Bubble, you have to find a Blue Bubble immediately.
Additionally, Fairy Ponds, Potion, and Triforce Segments will return the use of
your sword.

+---------------+
|--= Darknut =--|
+---------------+

DESCRIPTION: "The knight who lives in the labyrinths. He has lots of attacking
power. He repels Link's attacks from the front with his shield."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: You'll start to encounter these guys about halfway through the
game, but they're really not that tough to beat. You can't attack them head on,
since they're VERY effective with their shields, so you need to get around them
to the side or behind them and take some shots then. Two hits with the White
Sword is enough to take them out. Be warned, they will often change direction
randomly and run into you while you're trying to skirt around them. They won't
actively attack you but running into them will still do damage to the tune of
one full heart with no rings equipped. 

+-----------+
|--= Gel =--|
+-----------+

DESCRIPTION: "Jelly-like monsters that walk about bouncing around in the
labyrinths. When Link cuts Zol, it splits into two Gels. Gel has little
attacking power, but Zol has twice the power of Gels."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: These little slimy bastards can't really do much of anything
but bounce around and get killed. They have virtually no attack power and it
only takes one slash with the Wooden Sword to take them out. So, kill them and
grab whatever they drop.

+-------------+
|--= Ghini =--|
+-------------+

DESCRIPTION: "The ghost who lives in the graveyard. There are two types. There
are Ghinis who are there from the beginning of the game, and those who appear
when Link touches the gravestones. Ghinis have about the same attacking force
as Armos."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Ghinis are found only in the graveyards around Hyrule, so you
don't have to worry about bumping into one anywhere else. That being said, they
are one of the more difficult enemies you'll face in this game. They move slow
and don't have much of an attack, but if you touch them it'll inflict a fair
amount of damage. They can also take quite a walloping, so just whack them
around until they die and try to not touch them. They often drop rupees and
other valuables, so they're worth killing if you're strapped for cash.

+-------------+
|--= Gibdo =--|
+-------------+

DESCRIPTION: "The mummy man. He's got some strange powers, and some pretty
powerful attacking force."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Don't let the quote fool you, Gibdos aren't much of an
adversary. They don't have any real attacks. If they touch you, they'll do some
damage though. They move around in packs and have a fast/sporadic movement to
them, so play keep away while dealing with a group of them. Hit them with a few
slashes then back off and don't get bopped.

+--------------+
|--= Goriya =--|
+--------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A little devil that lives underground. He uses boomerangs. There
are two of his type, blue ones and red ones. Watch out for the blue ones! They
are strong."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Goriya attack the same way, regardless of their color: with
the Boomerang. And they're damn effective with it at that. The best strategy is
to keep away from their boomerang as best you can and try to get behind them to
hack away with your sword. Alternatively, the Bow and Arrow provides an
effective strategy for damage while staying at range. And if you're anywhere
near as good with the Boomerang as they are, you could use it to stun them and
then slash them with the sword.

+-------------+
|--= Keese =--|
+-------------+

DESCRIPTION: "Vire is a devil that controls the Keeses. When Link cuts it with
his sword, it turns into two Keeses. Keeses have little attacking power, but
Vire is a little stronger.
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Keese are very weak and very annoying. They're small and fast
and sometimes unpredictable. They're basically bats and they're always in
groups (and they tend to attack as a swarm as well). Simple slashing is the
best way to kill them, just pay attention to their flight patterns and stay on
your toes.

+---------------+
|--= Lanmola =--|
+---------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A gigantic centipede. Attack his head won't work. Boy! Does he
move fast!"
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Lanmolas are only found in the final Labyrinth, so you don't
have to worry about them until then. Though, once you do have to worry about
them, it's a damn battle. They're larger, faster, and stronger than Moldorms,
meaning they pack a punch and do so quickly. To defeat them you have to keep
hitting them with your sword to knock out segments of their body until only
the head remains and then you can kill the head (which moves very fast and is
hard to hit). 

+--------------+
|--= Leever =--|
+--------------+

DESCRIPTION: "They live in the ground and eat up the energy of creatures that
approach them. Blue Leevers are a little stronger, but the red ones don't
have much attack power."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Leevers are very common around Hyrule, especially in areas
with water. They dig into the ground and then come up in a completely different
area, making them difficult to keep track of. They can also take quite a few
hits to kill so it's best to avoid them until you feel like you can take them
on.

+-----------------+
|--= Like Like =--|
+-----------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A tube-like monster that has a soft spot for magic shields - he
eats them up."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: The most annoying enemy in the entire game by a fairly large
margin simply because they can wind up costing you quite a bit of money. If a
Like Like manages to touch you (and if you have a Magic Shield equipped), they
will eat your shield and you won't be able to get it back. It takes five hits
with the White Sword to kill them so be careful if you plan on engaging them.

+-------------+
|--= Lynel =--|
+-------------+

DESCRIPTION: "The guardian who attacks all those who come near Death Mountain.
Watch out! He's pretty strong, and Link's little shield can't stop his sword."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Basically giant beastly centaur things, Lynels are one of the
strongest enemies in the entire game. They wield swords and can shoot sword
beams at you that do a helluva lot of damage. So, they win the range game and
the power game. Early in the game, you should just avoid them. Later on, you
can better face them and they'll sometimes drop nice goodies for you.

+--------------+
|--= Moblin =--|
+--------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A bulldog-like goblin who lives in the forest. He attacks by
throwing spears. A little bit meaner than Octorok."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Moblins don't have much attack power and have even less
health, but they're somehow still annoying little creatures. They're real
advantage is being able to throw their spear across the entire screen with
laser accuracy. Though, their spears can be blocked with either of the game's
shields provided you're facing the correct way. A combination of blocking and
slashing is best for these guys and they'll usually drop some rupees or
something when they die.

+---------------+
|--= Moldorm =--|
+---------------+

DESCRIPTION: "The huge worm living in the labyrinths. It grows smaller as
Link attacks. Not so strong."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: A big worm thing that's got a body made of fireball looking
segments. Every hit takes away at least one segment (and one hit could take
all segments in a single slash if it's a good enough hit) until there's none
of it left. Patience is key here. Avoid getting hit as you slash away at it
and be wary of its seemingly random direction changes.

+---------------+
|--= Octorok =--|
+---------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A type of octopus that lives above ground. There are two types,
red and blue. Watch out for the blue ones. They're mean. They spit out rocks
at Link."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: The most generic of all the enemies, you'll find them
EVERYWHERE. The strategy here is easy: deflect their projectiles with your
shield and get close enough to whack them with your sword. Red Octoroks are
weaker than Blue Octoroks insofar as it takes less hits to kill them, but
they both have the same attack power. However, once you get the White Sword,
both Red and Blue Octoroks die from a single hit.

+-------------+
|--= Patra =--|
+-------------+

DESCRIPTION: "The Patra attack in groups, in two types of formations. Both
formation groups are strong. So be on your toes!"
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Patras are only found in the final Labyrinth of the game.
They are total pains to go up against (seriously, get the red ring) and guard
key areas of Death Mountain, so you have to fight them. They're encircled by
pieces of debris that protect them from sustaining damage until all of the
debris has been dispatched. Getting hit by the debris also inflicts quite a
bit of damage, so be careful around them. When all the debris is cleared, you
can move in and damage the eyeball to kill the Patra, which takes three hits
with the Magical Sword.

+--------------+
|--= Peahat =--|
+--------------+

DESCRIPTION: "Has little attacking power. This is the ghost of a flower that
bounces and flutters around the place. Link can eliminate it only when it's
standing still."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: These can be frustrating since you can only damage them when
they're not moving and they're rarely not moving. It's preferable to me to
avoid them altogether if I can, but if you want to take them out, just follow
carefully until they stop moving briefly and slash away. In my opinion, it's
way more effort than it's worth to kill these guys. And even if they do hit
you, they don't do a lot of damage.

+------------------+
|--= Pols Voice =--|
+------------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A ghost with big ears and a weak point - he hates loud noise."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Essentially a large free-moving rabbit's head that hops around
the room looking for its next victim. They will do massive damage if they
manage to touch Link, so play keep away with them. They can jump over barrier,
rivers, and other obstacles so your best bet is to kill them quickly. They're
much harder to avoid when they attack in a group, which they often do, so keep
your wits and take them out one by one before they have a chance to attack.

+------------+
|--= Rock =--|
+------------+

DESCRIPTION: "These rocks crumble off Death Mountain and fall down to attack
Link. He can't destroy these natural nuisances."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Do not ask me why a literal falling rock (that's really all it
is) is included in the games list of enemies, but it is. It's just a rock. You
can't fight it, you can't beat it, you can only avoid it. Good luck.

+------------+
|--= Rope =--|
+------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A poisonous snake that has made the labyrinth its home. It senses
other creatures quickly and suddenly comes after them (and Link, for that
matter!) once it has found them out. This one hasn't got a lot of attacking
power."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: You'll find Ropes in pretty much every single Labyrinth,
they're very common. They don't really have an attack and are super weak, so
you can just kill them with the sword pretty easily. They do move quite rapidly
across their rooms and are often found in groups, which can make them more
formidable. Still, you shouldn't have very many issues.
In Second Quest, there is a new type of Rope: Electrified Rope. They are the
same as normal ropes just electric and do more damage.

+---------------+
|--= Stalfos =--|
+---------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A skeleton that's got a sword in each hand. Little attacking
power."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Only in Zelda could a hopping rabbit head mess your shit up
while a dual-wielding skeleton poses very little threat. Stalfos really aren't
that tough. They do negligible damage and hardly ever attack. Instead, they
try to run into you, which also does very little damage. So smack them around
with your trusty sword and enjoy the free loot from a very non-menacing enemy.
In Second Quest, they can throw their swords at you which makes them a bit more
of a threat.

+--------------------+
|--= Stone Statue =--|
+--------------------+

DESCRIPTION: "Somebody placed these in the labyrinths a long time ago. They
suddenly attack Link when he approaches them. So you've really got to watch
out!"
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Statues can't really be killed, which makes them a royal pain
in the ass. Whenever you're in a room with them, they'll constantly pepper you
with fireballs (which can be deflected by your shield). Just get whatever you
need to get done around them done and move on.

+---------------+
|--= Tektite =--|
+---------------+

DESCRIPTION: "These spidery things jump all over the place. Red ones move about
a lot and blue ones only move a little. Tektites have little fighting power."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Tektites, much like the Octoroks, are everywhere. But they're
also very easy to dispatch. They don't have projectiles or anything of that
nature, their only attack is to jump at you and hit you. Get close and take
them out with your sword.

+-------------+
|--= Traps =--|
+-------------+

DESCRIPTION: "Somebody placed these in the labyrinths a long time ago. They
suddenly attack Link when he approaches them. So you've really got to watch
out!"
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Traps are very similar to Stone Statues in that they're in
pretty much every Labyrinth and can't be defeated, or stopped, or stunned, or
affected in any way. When you walk in front of a Trap, they shoot you with
impressive speed and will do pretty dang good damage. They're especially
annoying when they're on either side of Link for a nice little sandwich effect.
The best approach to Traps is to trigger them and then move back out of the
way.

+------------+
|--= Vire =--|
+------------+

DESCRIPTION: "Vire is a devil that controls the Keeses. When Link cuts it with
his sword, it turns into two Keeses. Keeses have little attacking power, but
Vire is a little stronger."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Vires are basically larger Keese. And by that, I mean much
larger and much stronger to the point of actually posing a threat on occasion.
When they're in the room, they'll try to run into you and can actually inflict
some decent damage. When you hit them, they'll split into Red Keese that move
faster but are more easily dispatched and not as aggressive.

+-------------------+
|--= Wall Master =--|
+-------------------+

DESCRIPTION: "A monster hand that appears out of the labyrinth wall. If it
catches Link, it takes him back to the entrance of the labyrinth."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: You need to be on your guard at pretty much all times through
the Labyrinths to avoid getting nabbed by a Wall Master. They're quite fond of
rooms just before the boss area, adding that insult to the injury if they
manage to grab you. Conveniently, you don't have to do the things you've
already done if they take you to the start of the Labyrinth, it's still
generally inconvenient tracing your way back through the Labyrinth at all.
Attacking them is a gamble that rarely pays off and usually ends with you at
the start of the Labyrinth. Best to just play keep away.

+----------------+
|--= Wizzrobe =--|
+----------------+

DESCRIPTION: "The Master of Movement. He appears here and there letting out
magic spells that Link's little shield can't hold back. He's pretty strong.
Watch out!"
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: If you haven't muttered "Fuck Wizzrobes" under your breath a
dozen times by the time you're through with this game, then I don't believe you
even played it. They are the worst, quite literally. They are the most annoying
and difficult enemy in this game (and that's including the bosses on that
list). They just suck, plain and simple. They come in two versions: Red and
Blue. The Red Wizzrobe can be killed in one hit with the Magical Sword if you
can pin him down long enough but shoots devastatingly powerful magic that'll
take multiple hearts with one blow. He disappears immediately after shooting
and reappears to start the cycle again. The Blue Wizzrobe take three hits from
the Magical Sword and teleport more often, but they are more visible during
their teleportation and therefore easier to predict. Occasionally, they'll
shoot a rapid burst of magical energy at Link that'll wipe you out completely
if it gets you. The Magical Shield can block their attacks, so block their
attack and attack them quickly to stand a chance here. If you aren't on your
game with these guys they will mess your shit up and that's a promise.

+-----------+
|--= Zol =--|
+-----------+

DESCRIPTION: "Jelly-like monsters that walk about bouncing around in the
labyrinths. When Link cuts Zol, it splits into two Gels. Gel has little
attacking power, but Zol has twice the power of Gel."
LOCATION: Underworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: Zols are literally just bigger Gels, and they're just as easy.
They're a bit quicker, but it's no big deal. It's a one-hit-kill with the White
Sword and it won't even split into Gels.

+------------+
|--= Zola =--|
+------------+

DESCRIPTION: "Half-fish, half-woman who lives in the water. When she sticks her
head out of the water, she lets out a ball that Link's little shield can't hold
back."
LOCATION: Overworld.
BATTLE STRATEGY: You'll encounter the Zola fairly early on. While you 
technically can kill it with your sword, it's better to wait until you have the
Bow and Arrow to do some real damage. The Wooden Shield is incapable of
blocking the Zola's projectiles, but the Magical Shield can no problem. Just
avoid until you can take it out.


   /\=====================================================================/\
  /__\------------------------={  B O S S E S  }=------------------------/__\
 /\  /\                             [BGBAD]                             /\  /\
/__\/__\===============================================================/__\/__\

    _____________________________________
   /  BOSS BATTLE: A Q U A M E N T U S   \_________________________________
  |------------------------------------------------------------------------\
  |                                                |                        |
  |  "A type of dragon that some call a unicorn.   | Received:              |
  |  As well as having lots of attack power, it's  |  -- Heart Container    |
  |  a fearful opponent. It emits beams."          |  -- Triforce Piece 1   |
  |                                                |                        |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Attacks:                                                               |
  |  - Shoots a burst of three fireballs at you. Each fireball does a       |
  |    full heart of damage with no rings equipped.                         |
  |  - That's it.                                                           |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Strategy:                                                              |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - If you have full heart containers going into the fight, just sit in  |
  |    the back and shoot sword beams at him. He'll die after a few hits.   |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - The other strategy is to wait for him to fire a volley of fireballs, |
  |    dodge the projectiles, and then run up close and slash him. In my    |
  |    opinion, this is quicker and easier than shooting sword beams.       |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - If you have the White Sword, he'll die after three hits.             |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - Beyond shooting fireballs, he barely even moves. He's a very         |
  |    stationary boss, so use that to your advantage when going in for     |
  |    the kill.                                                            |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - Once you have the Bow and Arrow, you can just stay back and shoot    |
  |    him in the head three times.                                         |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Summary:                                                               |
  |                                                                         |
  |  Aquamentus is a very easy boss (not surprising considering he's the    |
  |  first boss of the game. Shoot him with sword beams or wait for         |
  |  fireball volley and run up to slash him. You should be able to kill    |
  |  him without much fuss and get on to other things.                      |
   \_______________________________________________________________________/

    _______________________________
   /  BOSS BATTLE: D O D O N G O   \_______________________________________
  |------------------------------------------------------------------------\
  |                                                |                        |
  |  "A giant rhinoceros. It hasn't got so much    | Received:              |
  |  attacking power, but it bounces off attacks   |  -- Heart Container    |
  |  with its thick hide"                          |  -- Triforce Piece 2   |
  |                                                |                        |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Attacks:                                                               |
  |  - Just like the description says, the Dodongo doesn't have much        |
  |    attacking power, in that it doesn't attack at all.                   |
  |  - He just walks around the room.                                       |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Strategy:                                                              |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - The Dodongo is impervious to everything in your arsenal except bombs |
  |    but you probably guessed that cause the Labyrinth gave you bombs     |
  |    twice and you were smart enough to figure out the Old Man's clue.    |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - As the Dodongo walks around the room, lay a bomb in its path. As it  |
  |    walks over the bomb, it will eat it and then the bomb will explode   |
  |    inside it. Do this twice and the Dodongo will perish.                |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - If for whatever reason the Dodongo doesn't eat your bomb, the smoke  |
  |    will still stun it (this is what the Old Man was talking about) and  |
  |    you can run up and slash him to bits during that window.             |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Summary:                                                               |
  |                                                                         |
  |  Dodongo is probably the easiest boss in this game. Drop bombs in his   |
  |  path twice or stun him with smoke and hack away with your sword. This  |
  |  is an easy win so dispatch him and I'll see you on the other side.     |
   \_______________________________________________________________________/

    ___________________________________
   /  BOSS BATTLE: M A N H A N D L A   \___________________________________
  |------------------------------------------------------------------------\
  |                                                |                        |
  |  "A large man-eating flower with hands         | Received:              |
  |  sticking out in all four directions. It moves |  -- Heart Container    |
  |  faster as it loses hands. It's pretty mean.   |  -- Triforce Piece 3   |
  |  So watch out!"                                |                        |
  |                                                |                        |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Attacks:                                                               |
  |  - It'll charge at you with flailing arms and give you a good whack.    |
  |  - It also shoots fireballs from every orifice, of which there are a    |
  |    good number.                                                         |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Strategy:                                                              |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - There's one surefire way to kill the Manhandla with a single blow.   |
  |    You need to drop a bomb in its path in just the right way that it    |
  |    will explode when the Manhandla is centered on it. This will blow    |
  |    all of its limbs off in one fell swoop and that'll be that. You need |
  |    to be accurate with your bombs. It's much easier said than done.     |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - The actual strategy here is to hack off its limbs with your sword    |
  |    (two hits per limb with the White Sword). It'll speed up as you      |
  |    delimb it until all of its arms have been cut off.                   |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Summary:                                                               |
  |                                                                         |
  |  Manhandla is a real slapper. Try to nail it with a bomb in dead center |
  |  to blow all its limbs off or hack away at the arms with your sword.    |
  |  It shouldn't give you too much trouble.                                |
   \_______________________________________________________________________/

    _____________________________
   /  BOSS BATTLE: G L E E O K   \_________________________________________
  |------------------------------------------------------------------------\
  |                                                |                        |
  |  "A huge dragon that has 2 to 4 heads and      | Received:              |
  |  spits out beams at Link. Heads that Link cuts |  -- Heart Container    |
  |  off from its body fly around in the air.      |  -- Triforce Piece 3   |
  |                                                |                        |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Attacks:                                                               |
  |  - In this specific case we're dealing with a two-head Gleeok. The two  |
  |    heads will shoot fireballs at you.                                   |
  |  - Once you separate a head, the head will turn red and fly around the  |
  |    room shooting fireballs at you.                                      |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Strategy:                                                              |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - Make sure you've got a decent bit of health going into the fight.    |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - If you have full health, use your sword beams from range to do the   |
  |    bulk of the work.                                                    |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - If you don't, you'll have to get in close and just trade blows with  |
  |    him. Be consistent with your attacks and Gleeok will die before you  |
  |    do.                                                                  |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - I know that's not much of a strategy but don't blame me, blame the   |
  |    game designers.                                                      |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Summary:                                                               |
  |                                                                         |
  |  Gleeok is basically just a multi-headed, more annoying version of      |
  |  Aquamentus. Use your sword beams from range if you have full health,   |
  |  otherwise get in close and trade blows with it. You should be coming   |
  |  out the other side in no time.                                         |
   \_______________________________________________________________________/

    __________________________________
   /  BOSS BATTLE: D I G D O G G E R  \____________________________________
  |------------------------------------------------------------------------\
  |                                                |                        |
  |  "Big sea urchins. In spite of their big       | Received:              |
  |  bodies, they shrivel up when attacked. But    |  -- Heart Container    |
  |  watch out! They come on pretty strong."       |  -- Triforce Piece 3   |
  |                                                |                        |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Attacks:                                                               |
  |  - Digdogger doesn't really have any attacks, it just constantly moves  |
  |    around the room. If it touches you, it will do damage.               |
  |  - Also watch out for the four statues in the corner that will be       |
  |    continuously shooting fire at you                                    |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Strategy:                                                              |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - Digdogger's strategy makes him one of the easiest bosses in the      |
  |    game. Make sure you have your Recorder equipped and play it during   |
  |    the fight.                                                           |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - The Recorder melody will cause Digdogger to shrivel up to a tiny,    |
  |    much less threatening size. Once he's been shrunk down, two slashes  |
  |    with the Magical Sword will take him out.                            |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - Digdogger moves pretty fast once it's been shrunk down. You can use  |
  |    the Boomerang to stun it and keep it in place while you whack at it. |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - You'll need to be evading the Stone Statue fireballs the entire      |
  |    time, cause they'll just keep peppering you. They're honestly a      |
  |    bigger threat that Digdogger.                                        |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Summary:                                                               |
  |                                                                         |
  |  Digdogger is a giant floating booger and a scaredy-cat. Play your      |
  |  Recorder to shrink it down and then hit it with a Boomerang and hack   |
  |  it to bits. A quick jam session and you'll be outta there in no time.  |
   \_______________________________________________________________________/

    __________________________
   /  BOSS BATTLE: G O H M A  \____________________________________________
  |------------------------------------------------------------------------\
  |                                                |                        |
  |  "The super huge crab that lives in the        | Received:              |
  |  labyrinths. Its hard shell will repulse any   |  -- Heart Container    |
  |  attack. Attack its weak point with a special  |  -- Triforce Piece 3   |
  |  weapon."                                      |                        |
  |                                                |                        |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Attacks:                                                               |
  |  - Gohma will run back and forth at the top of her little lair and      |
  |    try to warm you up with some fireballs.                              |
  |  - That's pretty much it.                                               |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Strategy:                                                              |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - Strafe and use your shield to block all of the incoming fireballs.   |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - Wait for Gohma to descend from the top and open her eye, then shoot  |
  |    her in the eye with an Arrow. She'll die from one shot.              |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - If you're out of rupees (and thus arrows), you literally can't use   |
  |    anything else, so find some rupees ASAP.                             |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Summary:                                                               |
  |                                                                         |
  |  Gohma's a crabby bitch that hangs in the back and peppers you with     |
  |  fire. Teach her a lesson by shooting her in the eye with an arrow.     |
  |  You should be able to kill her almost as soon as you walk through the  |
  |  door so she's a quick one.                                             |
   \_______________________________________________________________________/

    ___________________________
   /  BOSS BATTLE: G A N O N   \___________________________________________
  |------------------------------------------------------------------------\
  |                                                |                        |
  |  ""Link's going to have a difficult time       | Received:              |
  |  trying to destroy Ganon. He's real mean. But  |  -- Princess Zelda     |
  |  even Ganon has his weak point.                |  -- Triforce           |
  |                                                |                        |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Attacks:                                                               |
  |  - Disappears and shoots unblockable fireballs at you.                  |
  |  - That's it.                                                           |
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Strategy:                                                              |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - You CAN walk on the black parts of this room. The tiles are just for |
  |    decoration. The whole room is solid.                                 |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - While Ganon is fighting like a bitch and being invisible, you gotta  |
  |    find him. Stab blindly around the room until you hit him. He'll      |
  |    appear briefly and then disappear again. Do this four times.         |
  |                                                                         |
  |  - After the fourth hit, Ganon will turn brown-ish and that's your      |
  |    cue. Shoot him with a Silver Arrow and he'll turn to ash.            | 
  |                                                                         |
  |-------------------------------------------------------------------------|
  |                                                                         |
  |  Summary:                                                               |
  |                                                                         |
  |  Ganon's a chump. Whack around blindly with the sword until you hit him |
  |  four times then shoot him with a silver arrow. He's no real threat at  |
  |  all which kinda leaves you wondering how Hyrule ever got into this     |
  |  mess in the first place.                                               |
   \_______________________________________________________________________/

world. Each shop holds three items. Not all items are the same price at each
shop, so you can shop around and find better prices for items you need (or
just look below and see where to go. Each shop contains a set of coordinates
to help you locate it using the map included in the Maps section of this guide.
Regarding the items in each shop, they are listed individually under the shop
header with their price in rupees next to the item in parentheses.

   /\=====================================================================/\
  /__\-----------------={  T I P S   &   T R I C K S  }=-----------------/__\
 /\  /\                             [TRICK]                             /\  /\
/__\/__\===============================================================/__\/__\

Below you will find a number of tricks that you can use to either exploit the
game to your advantage or just make it a bit more easy or convenient. Let's dig
in.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
                        T H E   " Z E L D A "   N A M E
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In an effort to further the confusion regarding Link's name, Nintendo have seen
fit to throw this little trick in here. If you enter your player name as
"ZELDA", you will automatically skip the First Quest and start fresh on the
Second Quest. So, if you want to just skip the quite easy First Quest and get
straight to the more challenging Second Quest, that's how.

Additionally, you still have three character spaces left after "ZELDA". As long
as the first five characters spell "ZELDA" you can put whatever you like for
the last three characters and the trick will still work.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   T H I N G S   T O   D O   W I T H   A   S E C O N D   C O N T R O L L E R
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are a few things you can do with a second controller connected (no
multiplayer, sorry).

1. While in your inventory, if you press UP + A on the Controller 2, it will
bring up the Save menu.

2. If you do the Save menu while in a Labyrinth and select "Continue", it will
take you to the beginning of the Labyrinth with three hearts.

3. You can also use the Save trick to cheat a little bit at the Gambling game.
I touch on this in the Rupee Farming section.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
                    R E G A R D I N G   T H E   S W I T C H
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Switch's Suspend feature can be used very usefully throughout Zelda and is
basically a one-up to the NES style save. The Suspend creates a suspended save 
of your game exactly as it is when you create the save. NOTHING will change,
not even RNG elements.

This can be used to attempt particularly difficult things over and over again.
Or it can be used to cheat like a psychic at the Gambling Game. Simply go into
a Gambling Den, then create a suspend save, pick one of the options and IF you
don't get it pay attention to which choice was the winner, reload your suspend
save and pick that choice because it won't change. Use this to guarantee a win
every time and bank up rupees fast.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
                      C O N T R O L   Y O U R   E N E M Y
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Clearing out all of the enemies on a single screen will cause that screen to be
empty for a bit. But after a while, the enemies will all spawn back in at once.
However, if you leave one enemy alive on a screen, then the other enemies will
never respawn (unless you die). IMPORTANT NOTE: Zolas do not contribute to this
trick.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
                    D A R K N U T S   &   W I Z Z R O B E S
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Darknuts and Wizzrobes are easily the two worst enemies in the game. By a lot.
But there are some tricks you can use to make them a bit less of a pain in the
ass.

Darknuts: It's always better to attack a Darknut from the side than from
behind. The odds are against you and they will often do a complete about face
when you're behind them. It's always better to be at the side. Also, Darknuts
only turn when they are on a square. Link however can stand on the tile lines.
So, you can stand on the lines and attack them from the side for a bit of an
easier time.

Wizzrobes: The safest place in all of the Legend of Zelda is the doorways
between Labyrinth rooms. You can stand in the doorway and fire your sword beams
to kill everything in the room. This goes especially for taking care of
Wizzrobes. Use this trick to take care of all the Yellow Wizzrobes in any room.
Once you've got it down to just Blue Wizzrobes, leave the room and come back.
As long as you had more than one Blue Wizzrobe in there when you left, they
will be Yellow Wizzrobes when you come back in.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
                  T R I C K S   W I T H   A   R E C O R D E R
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Recorder is the most useful of all tools in Link's. It has a number of
magical effects when you play it.

The Recorder will heal any jinxes put on Link by flashing Bubbles.

Using the Recorder on any screen where there is not a hidden entrance will
spawn a whirlwind that will allow you to warp around Hyrule, putting you at the
entrance to any Labyrinth you've already completed. It will always warp you
to the entrance of the First Quest Labyrinths, even during the Second Quest.
This is especially useful after clearing the Z Labyrinth in Second Quest since
the Recorder will take you to the location of the Lizard Labyrinth which is
a Fairy Pond in Second Quest.

You can control where you warp to with the direction you are facing. If you
face north or east, it will take you to the next Labyrinth in the sequence
(i.e. from Eagle to Moon). If you face south or west, it will take you to the
previous Labyrinth in the sequence (i.e. from Moon to Eagle). Additionally,
playing the Recorder multiple times while the Whirlwind approaches will jump
that many sequences (i.e. face north and play the recorder three times to jump
from Eagle to Snake). Also, if you complete the dungeons out of order, the
uncompleted dungeons will be skipped automatically in the sequence.

And that's all I have to say about that.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
                     E N E M Y   D R O P   P A T T E R N S
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There are certain ways that you can attempt to control the what the enemies you
kill drop for you in an effort to curate your loot to get the things you need.
These aren't something that I found myself through trial and error (that would
take forever), though some of them are things that you will eventually notice.
Others I saw on the forums at GameFAQs and have since forgotten who the posters
where that discovered this information (Sorry! If this is you, PLEASE email me
with proof so I can give you proper credit).

+----------------------+
|--= THE 10TH ENEMY =--|
+----------------------+

There's an Old Man screen that gives you the hint "10TH ENEMY HAS THE BOMB". He
is telling you about this little trick. If you kill 10 enemies without taking
damage AND kill the tenth enemy with a bomb, then the last enemy will drop a
pack of bombs for you. It's useful (I guess?) but often more pain than it's
worth as I never really had a problem with bomb supply through either Quest.

IMPORTANT NOTE: Keese, Gels, Like Likes, Armos, Gleeok Heads, Digdoggers,
Bubbles, and Petra children do not contribute to the enemy count for this.

If you finish off the tenth enemy with anything other than a bomb, you'll get a
five-rupee piece instead (way more useful in my opinion).

+------------------------+
|--= ENEMY BOMB DROPS =--|
+------------------------+

Also dealing with bomb drops here. Bomb drops occur in a fixed pattern with the
following enemies: Blue Octoroks, Blue Moblins, Blue Lynels, Vires, Red
Darknuts, Red Goriyas, Gibdos, and Red Wizzrobes. Meaning, you can control
whether or not you receive bombs when killing these enemies. The first, sixth,
and eight kills of the enemies listed above (can chain the enemies together,
meaning you don't have to kill just one enemy variety per chain) will drop
bombs and the cycle will repeat every 10 kills.

+--------------------------------------+
|--= 16 KILLS WITHOUT TAKING DAMAGE =--|
+--------------------------------------+

If you can manage to kill 16 enemies without taking a single bit of damage, the
16th enemy will drop a Fairy as a reward. Just like the 10th Enemy trick: Keese
Gels, Like Likes, Armos, Gleeok Heads, Digdogger, Bubbles, and Petra children
do not count towards this.

+---------------------+
|--= COUNTER RESET =--|
+---------------------+

The kill counter will reset for every instance of the following:

 - the game is powered on
 - the game is reset
 - Link takes damage
 - Link dies

That's it, otherwise your counter is ticking up.


   /\=====================================================================/\
  /__\------------------------={  C H E A T S  }=------------------------/__\

   /\=====================================================================/\
  /__\-----------------={  R U P E E   F A R M I N G  }=-----------------/__\
 /\  /\                             [RUPEE]                             /\  /\
/__\/__\===============================================================/__\/__\

There are several good locations and methods to farm for rupees. Here we'll
cover the most effective three methods (in my opinion, which is fact).

+----------------+
|--= THE LOOP =--|
+----------------+

I cover this in the Walkthrough, but we'll go over it again here. If you head
right all the way from the origin point (H8) until you can't anymore (H16), you
will encounter a lot of lucrative and easy enemies on the way. Lots of Leevers,
Tektites, and Octoroks. The more you kill without taking damage, the more
rupees you will have dropped for you. This is the best area in my opinion to
farm for rupees because the Tektites and Leevers are very easy to continuously
kill without taking damage. One the way back from H16, you can head north one
at H12 into G12 and kill the Moblins and Octoroks from G12 to G9 before heading
down to H9 to make it more of a loop. So: H9 to H16, H16 to H12, up to G12, G12
to G9, down to H9, and loop.

+---------------------+
|--= THE GRAVEYARD =--|
+---------------------+

In the graveyard, the Ghinis make a nice farming option. Equip your boomerang
and use it to stun the single Ghini in any screen. Then run into as many of the
tombstones as you can manage. Each one will spawn another Ghini, but they won't
take any damage. They can only be killed by defeating the original Ghini, which
you stunned with the Boomerang. Keep track of it and take it out to kill all
the Ghinis, each of which will drop something for you, usually rupees.

+----------------------------------+
|--= CHEATING THE GAMBLING GAME =--|
+----------------------------------+

This method requires using the second controller Save trick. Get bombs and save
your game. Head west one from the origin to H7. Bomb the north wall five tiles
to the left of the north path to open the cave for the Gambling game. Head in
and play the game. If you win, save the game. If you lose, you can select
"Retry" to reload your save. Do this as many times as you need, and you should
have 255 rupees shortly.

And finally, the moment you've all been waiting for: Herc's opinion. It has
been said that Herc's opinion is so devastatingly accurate at all times that
every word from his mouth ought to be considered fact. And in that regard, it's
time for me to drop some fact bombs about this game and what I think of it.

The Legend of Zelda spawned an epic, sweeping gaming franchise the likes of
which have barely been replicated by anyone else to this day. Bearing that in
mind, it's quite tough to look at this game objectively 30 years later. For the
time, it was a masterpiece of game design that pushed the boundaries of what
the current generation of consoles could do.

That being said, you certainly feel the limitations of this era's game designs
while playing through the Legend of Zelda in the modern era. The lack of
diagonal mobility and frustratingly designed enemies can make the Legend of
Zelda annoying, albeit in very brief windows. The reuse of bosses and lame
recycling of upgrade versions of items you already have (that seem to have been
downgraded specifically so the upgraded versions could exist at all) can dampen
the experience ever so slightly. But if you're someone who lets all of those
things get to you, then retro gaming just isn't for you at all.

For its time, the Legend of Zelda is a triumphant achievement. It's a joy to 
play and a challenge in the right ways (especially through the Second Quest).
Playing through it without a guide and finding your own way is not impossible
but it certainly makes the game tougher while also preserving the experience of
exploration. All in all, it's pretty much a masterpiece despite its flaws and
its highly revered by Zelda players across the world.

I give it a 9/10, it's a really fun game, slightly marred by a few questionable 
design choices, but nevertheless really enjoyable.

+--------------+
|--= FAQ 01 =--|
+--------------+

Q: I'm a parent and my child read your guide and it has bad words in it.
   How dare you?

A: There are several instances in this very guide where I mention that it
   will contain some content unsuitable for minors. Police what your children
   access on the internet if it's a major concern for you. It's not my job to
   control what your kids are looking at. Beyond that, I recognize this is at
   its core a game for children, so I've intentionally toned it down quite
   considerably. Besides, I read stuff like this and watched/played Rated R/M
   things when I was a kid. And I turned out alright, at least I think I did.

+--------------+
|--= FAQ 02 =--|
+--------------+

Q: The art in your guide is really cool, can I use it in mine?

A: I'd really rather you didn't. The detailed (and time-consuming) art is
   mostly what makes my guides stand out (that and my grade-A sense of humor).
   More importantly, I work hard on the ASCII art that's in my guides and it's
   not terribly difficult to learn how to do it. So, unfortunately, the answer
   to that is "no". The art is included in the copyright.

+--------------+
|--= FAQ 03 =--|
+--------------+

Q: Yo, what's up with the shape of the third Labyrinth? Are Nintendo racists?

A: No, Nintendo aren't racists. Yes, this dungeon is technically in the shape
of a swastika. No, it is NOT a swastika. It is actually a Manji. The Manji is a
character in the Buddhist philosophy/religion and represents the concept of
Dharma, universal harmony, and the balance of opposites. So, no Nintendo aren't
racists, since Buddhists are pretty much as far from racists as you can get.

Q: Okay, but they should have--

A: No, they shouldn't have. They're totally allowed to use the symbol of the 
Manji if they want. Let's also not forget that when this game first released,
Japan was in staunch denial of their participation in World War II (to this day
they still deny that the Nanking Massacre ever happened, which is shitty, I'll
grant you that), so it's not even remotely surprising that they would include
it without thinking about the association of the symbol outside of Japan.

Q: But the first dungeon is an eagle shape and that was also a Nazi symbol.

A: Why do you want Nintendo to be Nazis so damn bad? The Eagle is also an
American symbol. There's also a Tengu in Japanese mythology that looks a lot
like an eagle. Read a book and stop trying to make Nintendo look like Nazis.
Just stop it. Stop it right now.

+--------------+
|--= FAQ 04 =--|
+--------------+

Q: Why do you do so much before going to the first dungeon?

A: Why don't you? Getting all of that stuff before the first dungeon makes the
rest of the First Quest so much easier. You can seriously breeze through the
entire thing in an afternoon. You can upgrade your sword, get a better shield,
have three more hearts, and take half as much damage all before the first
dungeon. Why wouldn't you do that?

+--------------+
|--= FAQ 05 =--|
+--------------+

Q: I bought arrows, but now can't shoot any?

A: Arrows only work as long as you have rupees. Firing one arrow costs one
rupee. So as long as you have rupees, you have arrows. If you don't have any
rupees, you have no arrows. It's that simple.

+--------------+
|--= FAQ 06 =--|
+--------------+

Q: Why does my Blue Candle stop working after I shoot it?

A: Because that's it's one caveat. It only works once per screen. Nintendo
decided to limit the Blue Candle in this way so there would be a reason to want
the Red Candle that serves as a reward for completing the Demon Labyrinth.
